# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

- ReplicaFetcherThread, AbstractFetcherThread, ReplicaFetcherManager

- ReplicaState enum (TRUNCATING, FETCHING states)
- PartitionFetchState for partition-level fetch coordination

### **Protocol Flow** covering:
1. ReplicaFetcherThread initialization and partition assignment
2. Continuous fetching with epoch validation
3. Log truncation handling via OffsetTruncationState
4. ISR updates based on replica lag monitoring
5. High watermark advancement based on ISR confirmation
6. Persistence of epoch and offset information for recovery

The answer provides a complete view of Apache Kafka's sophisticated inter-broker replication protocol implementation across 25 core files.

\"text\": \"The Apache Kafka inter-broker replication protocol is implemented through a comprehensive set of Java and Scala classes in the sg-evals/kafka--0753c489 repository. The protocol orchestrates the replication of log segments from leader brokers to follower replicas across the cluster.\\n\\n## Core Replication Components\\n\\n### ReplicaFetcherThread (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaFetcherThread.scala)\\nThe primary component responsible for implementing the inter-broker replication protocol. This thread runs on follower brokers to fetch data from leader brokers. It extends AbstractFetcherThread and handles the actual fetching of records, managing replica state transitions, and truncating logs when necessary.\\n\\n### AbstractFetcherThread (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/AbstractFetcherThread.scala)\\nThe base class for ReplicaFetcherThread that provides the core fetching logic. Key features include:\\n- Management of partition fetch states (FETCHING, TRUNCATING)\\n- Handling of offset truncation via OffsetTruncationState case class\\n- Epoch-based truncation to handle leader changes\\n- Support for tiered storage via TierStateMachine integration\\n- Fetching request/response handling with fetch session optimization\\n\\n### ReplicaFetcherManager (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaFetcherManager.scala)\\nManages a pool of ReplicaFetcherThread instances, one per leader broker. Extends AbstractFetcherManager and creates fetcher threads that pull data from specific source brokers. It handles partition assignment and load distribution across multiple fetcher threads (configurable via num.replica.fetchers).\\n\\n## Partition State and ISR Management\\n\\n### Partition (core/src/main/scala/kafka/cluster/Partition.scala)\\nThe core component representing a partition on a broker. It manages:\\n- **ISR (In-Sync Replicas)**: The set of replicas that have caught up to the leader\\n- **ISR Expansion**: Adding replicas back to ISR via PendingExpandIsr when they catch up\\n- **ISR Shrinking**: Removing replicas from ISR via PendingShrinkIsr when they lag beyond replica.lag.time.max.ms\\n- **Partition State Hierarchy**:\\n  - PartitionState (sealed trait)\\n  - CommittedPartitionState: The acknowledged ISR state\\n  - PendingShrinkIsr: In-flight ISR shrink request to controller\\n  - PendingExpandIsr: In-flight ISR expand request to controller\\n- High watermark management and its relationship to replica lag\\n\\n## Log Offset and Epoch Tracking\\n\\n### LeaderEpochFileCache (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/epoch/LeaderEpochFileCache.java)\\nA Java class that caches leader epoch entries with their corresponding start offsets. This is critical for:\\n- Handling leader changes without data loss\\n- Determining the truncation point when a replica reconnects\\n- Supporting the epochForOffset() method to find the leader epoch for a given offset\\n- Persisting epoch information to disk for recovery\\n\\n### UnifiedLog (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/UnifiedLog.java)\\nThe unified log abstraction that manages:\\n- **logStartOffset**: The earliest valid offset in the log (may advance due to log retention or deletion)\\n- **leaderEpochCache**: Reference to LeaderEpochFileCache for epoch tracking\\n- **Truncation**: Truncating the log to a specific offset when a replica detects a divergence\\n- **High watermark management**: maybeUpdateHighWatermark() and updateHighWatermark() methods\\n- **Remote log integration**: Integration with RemoteLogManager for tiered storage\\n- **LogAppendInfo**: Tracking appended records with logStartOffset and other metadata\\n\\n## Replica State Tracking\\n\\n### Replica (server/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/replica/Replica.java)\\nTracks the state of individual replicas in the partition, including:\\n- lastCaughtUpTimeMs: When the replica last caught up to the leader\\n- logStartOffset and logEndOffsetMetadata: Offset ranges of the replica\\n- lastFetchLeaderLogEndOffset and lastFetchTimeMs: For lag calculation\\nThis state is used to determine ISR membership and detect lagging replicas.\\n\\n### ReplicaState (server/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/ReplicaState.java)\\nJava enum representing the state of a replica during fetching:\\n- TRUNCATING: Replica is truncating its log due to epoch change or offset divergence\\n- FETCHING: Replica is actively fetching records from the leader\\n\\n### PartitionFetchState (server/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/PartitionFetchState.java)\\nJava record class tracking the fetch state of a single partition:\\n- topicId, fetchOffset, currentLeaderEpoch\\n- state: ReplicaState (TRUNCATING or FETCHING)\\n- lastFetchedEpoch: For epoch tracking and truncation\\n- lag: Optional lag in bytes/messages\\n\\n## Endpoints and Communication\\n\\n### RemoteLeaderEndPoint (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/RemoteLeaderEndPoint.scala)\\nImplements the LeaderEndPoint trait for fetching from remote brokers. Communicates with leader brokers via BrokerBlockingSender and handles:\\n- Building fetch requests with proper offset and epoch information\\n- Processing fetch responses from remote brokers\\n- Handling various fetch errors (OFFSET_OUT_OF_RANGE, FENCED_LEADER_EPOCH, etc.)\\n\\n### LocalLeaderEndPoint (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/LocalLeaderEndPoint.scala)\\nImplements the LeaderEndPoint trait for local fetching (when leader and follower are on same broker). Used for tiered storage and replica migrations.\\n\\n### BrokerBlockingSender (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerBlockingSender.scala)\\nHandles the actual network communication with remote brokers, sending fetch requests and receiving responses.\\n\\n## Configuration and Additional Components\\n\\n### ReplicationConfigs (server/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/config/ReplicationConfigs.java)\\nDefines all replication-related configuration parameters:\\n- replica.fetch.max.bytes, replica.fetch.min.bytes\\n- replica.fetch.wait.max.ms: Must be <= replica.lag.time.max.ms to prevent ISR thrashing\\n- num.replica.fetchers: Number of parallel fetcher threads per broker\\n\\n### TierStateMachine (core/src/main/java/kafka/server/TierStateMachine.java)\\nManages the state transitions for tiered storage, handling the OFFSET_MOVED_TO_TIERED_STORAGE error and coordinating between local and remote log storage.\\n\\n### ReplicaAlterLogDirsThread and Manager\\nHandles moving replicas to different log directories, using similar fetching logic to ReplicaFetcherThread but with future log management.\\n\\n## Protocol Flow\\n\\n1. **Initialization**: ReplicaFetcherManager creates ReplicaFetcherThread instances for each leader broker\\n2. **Fetching**: Threads continuously call doWork() to fetch batches of records from leaders\\n3. **Truncation**: When encountering epoch mismatches (FENCED_LEADER_EPOCH), AbstractFetcherThread determines truncation offset using LeaderEpochFileCache\\n4. **State Tracking**: AbstractFetcherThread manages replica state (TRUNCATING/FETCHING) and updates PartitionFetchState\\n5. **ISR Updates**: ReplicaManager monitors replica lag via Replica.lastCaughtUpTimeMs and coordinates with the partition to expand/shrink ISR\\n6. **High Watermark**: ReplicaManager advances high watermark based on ISR replicas and partition log state\\n7. **Persistence**: LeaderEpochFileCache and LogOffsetSnapshot persist epoch and offset information for recovery\\n\\nThis multi-layered architecture ensures robust, efficient, and fault-tolerant inter-broker replication across the Kafka cluster.\"\n}\n",

\"text\": \"The Apache Kafka inter-broker replication protocol is implemented through a comprehensive set of Java and Scala classes in the sg-evals/kafka--0753c489 repository. The protocol orchestrates the replication of log segments from leader brokers to follower replicas across the cluster.\\n\\n## Core Replication Components\\n\\n### ReplicaFetcherThread (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaFetcherThread.scala)\\nThe primary component responsible for implementing the inter-broker replication protocol. This thread runs on follower brokers to fetch data from leader brokers. It extends AbstractFetcherThread and handles the actual fetching of records, managing replica state transitions, and truncating logs when necessary.\\n\\n### AbstractFetcherThread (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/AbstractFetcherThread.scala)\\nThe base class for ReplicaFetcherThread that provides the core fetching logic. Key features include:\\n- Management of partition fetch states (FETCHING, TRUNCATING)\\n- Handling of offset truncation via OffsetTruncationState case class\\n- Epoch-based truncation to handle leader changes\\n- Support for tiered storage via TierStateMachine integration\\n- Fetching request/response handling with fetch session optimization\\n\\n### ReplicaFetcherManager (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaFetcherManager.scala)\\nManages a pool of ReplicaFetcherThread instances, one per leader broker. Extends AbstractFetcherManager and creates fetcher threads that pull data from specific source brokers. It handles partition assignment and load distribution across multiple fetcher threads (configurable via num.replica.fetchers).\\n\\n## Partition State and ISR Management\\n\\n### Partition (core/src/main/scala/kafka/cluster/Partition.scala)\\nThe core component representing a partition on a broker. It manages:\\n- **ISR (In-Sync Replicas)**: The set of replicas that have caught up to the leader\\n- **ISR Expansion**: Adding replicas back to ISR via PendingExpandIsr when they catch up\\n- **ISR Shrinking**: Removing replicas from ISR via PendingShrinkIsr when they lag beyond replica.lag.time.max.ms\\n- **Partition State Hierarchy**:\\n  - PartitionState (sealed trait)\\n  - CommittedPartitionState: The acknowledged ISR state\\n  - PendingShrinkIsr: In-flight ISR shrink request to controller\\n  - PendingExpandIsr: In-flight ISR expand request to controller\\n- High watermark management and its relationship to replica lag\\n\\n## Log Offset and Epoch Tracking\\n\\n### LeaderEpochFileCache (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/epoch/LeaderEpochFileCache.java)\\nA Java class that caches leader epoch entries with their corresponding start offsets. This is critical for:\\n- Handling leader changes without data loss\\n- Determining the truncation point when a replica reconnects\\n- Supporting the epochForOffset() method to find the leader epoch for a given offset\\n- Persisting epoch information to disk for recovery\\n\\n### UnifiedLog (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/UnifiedLog.java)\\nThe unified log abstraction that manages:\\n- **logStartOffset**: The earliest valid offset in the log (may advance due to log retention or deletion)\\n- **leaderEpochCache**: Reference to LeaderEpochFileCache for epoch tracking\\n- **Truncation**: Truncating the log to a specific offset when a replica detects a divergence\\n- **High watermark management**: maybeUpdateHighWatermark() and updateHighWatermark() methods\\n- **Remote log integration**: Integration with RemoteLogManager for tiered storage\\n- **LogAppendInfo**: Tracking appended records with logStartOffset and other metadata\\n\\n## Replica State Tracking\\n\\n### Replica (server/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/replica/Replica.java)\\nTracks the state of individual replicas in the partition, including:\\n- lastCaughtUpTimeMs: When the replica last caught up to the leader\\n- logStartOffset and logEndOffsetMetadata: Offset ranges of the replica\\n- lastFetchLeaderLogEndOffset and lastFetchTimeMs: For lag calculation\\nThis state is used to determine ISR membership and detect lagging replicas.\\n\\n### ReplicaState (server/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/ReplicaState.java)\\nJava enum representing the state of a replica during fetching:\\n- TRUNCATING: Replica is truncating its log due to epoch change or offset divergence\\n- FETCHING: Replica is actively fetching records from the leader\\n\\n### PartitionFetchState (server/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/PartitionFetchState.java)\\nJava record class tracking the fetch state of a single partition:\\n- topicId, fetchOffset, currentLeaderEpoch\\n- state: ReplicaState (TRUNCATING or FETCHING)\\n- lastFetchedEpoch: For epoch tracking and truncation\\n- lag: Optional lag in bytes/messages\\n\\n## Endpoints and Communication\\n\\n### RemoteLeaderEndPoint (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/RemoteLeaderEndPoint.scala)\\nImplements the LeaderEndPoint trait for fetching from remote brokers. Communicates with leader brokers via BrokerBlockingSender and handles:\\n- Building fetch requests with proper offset and epoch information\\n- Processing fetch responses from remote brokers\\n- Handling various fetch errors (OFFSET_OUT_OF_RANGE, FENCED_LEADER_EPOCH, etc.)\\n\\n### LocalLeaderEndPoint (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/LocalLeaderEndPoint.scala)\\nImplements the LeaderEndPoint trait for local fetching (when leader and follower are on same broker). Used for tiered storage and replica migrations.\\n\\n### BrokerBlockingSender (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerBlockingSender.scala)\\nHandles the actual network communication with remote brokers, sending fetch requests and receiving responses.\\n\\n## Configuration and Additional Components\\n\\n### ReplicationConfigs (server/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/config/ReplicationConfigs.java)\\nDefines all replication-related configuration parameters:\\n- replica.fetch.max.bytes, replica.fetch.min.bytes\\n- replica.fetch.wait.max.ms: Must be <= replica.lag.time.max.ms to prevent ISR thrashing\\n- num.replica.fetchers: Number of parallel fetcher threads per broker\\n\\n### TierStateMachine (core/src/main/java/kafka/server/TierStateMachine.java)\\nManages the state transitions for tiered storage, handling the OFFSET_MOVED_TO_TIERED_STORAGE error and coordinating between local and remote log storage.\\n\\n### ReplicaAlterLogDirsThread and Manager\\nHandles moving replicas to different log directories, using similar fetching logic to ReplicaFetcherThread but with future log management.\\n\\n## Protocol Flow\\n\\n1. **Initialization**: ReplicaFetcherManager creates ReplicaFetcherThread instances for each leader broker\\n2. **Fetching**: Threads continuously call doWork() to fetch batches of records from leaders\\n3. **Truncation**: When encountering epoch mismatches (FENCED_LEADER_EPOCH), AbstractFetcherThread determines truncation offset using LeaderEpochFileCache\\n4. **State Tracking**: AbstractFetcherThread manages replica state (TRUNCATING/FETCHING) and updates PartitionFetchState\\n5. **ISR Updates**: ReplicaManager monitors replica lag via Replica.lastCaughtUpTimeMs and coordinates with the partition to expand/shrink ISR\\n6. **High Watermark**: ReplicaManager advances high watermark based on ISR replicas and partition log state\\n7. **Persistence**: LeaderEpochFileCache and LogOffsetSnapshot persist epoch and offset information for recovery\\n\\nThis multi-layered architecture ensures robust, efficient, and fault-tolerant inter-broker replication across the Kafka cluster.\"\n}\n",
